    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13724798372434047096">La mort est mon métier sont les pseudo-mémoires de Rudolf Höß (renommé Rudolf Lang dans l'ouvrage). Rudolf Höß était le commandant du camp de concentration et d'extermination d'Auschwitz pendant la Seconde Guerre mondiale.<br/><br/>L'histoire commence en 1913 alors que Rudolf Lang a 13 ans.<br/><br/>Il reçoit une éducation catholique mal comprise et très normative. Son père, un commerçant, ay</span>
  <span id="freeText13724798372434047096" style="display:none">La mort est mon métier sont les pseudo-mémoires de Rudolf Höß (renommé Rudolf Lang dans l'ouvrage). Rudolf Höß était le commandant du camp de concentration et d'extermination d'Auschwitz pendant la Seconde Guerre mondiale.<br /><br />L'histoire commence en 1913 alors que Rudolf Lang a 13 ans.<br /><br />Il reçoit une éducation catholique mal comprise et très normative. Son père, un commerçant, ayant reçu une éducation militaire (famille militaire), totalement psychorigide, qui a commis un péché dans sa jeunesse à Paris et avec qui il entretient des rapports tendus, veut qu'il devienne prêtre pour expier les fautes que lui-même a commises. Rudolf croit en Dieu, jusqu'au jour où, en se battant avec un de ses camarades d'école (Werner), il lui casse la jambe. Immédiatement, il va se confesser à un prêtre. Le soir même, son père devient fou de rage après avoir appris que son fils a commis un « péché » sans lui en parler. Rudolf se sent trahi par le prêtre, seule personne au courant de l'épisode, les autres croyant à un accident. Or, on apprendra que c'est en fait le père de l'enfant blessé qui s'est plaint devant une assemblée de parents d'élèves. Le mal est fait : Rudolf ne croit plus en Dieu. Son père meurt peu avant la déclaration de guerre en 1914.<br /><br />À seize ans, Lang débute sa carrière militaire, d'abord en partant directement pour le front Ouest où il sera intercepté puis renvoyé à l'arrière car il est trop jeune, puis comme aide à l'hôpital militaire où il rencontrera un dragon de cavalerie qui le persuadera de rentrer dans son unité et de partir sur le front en Turquie.<br /><br />À la fin de la guerre, il se retrouve au chômage, rejeté par sa famille. Il s'apprête à se suicider lorsqu'un de ses collègues arrive et lui brandit un tract en lui disant de ne pas trahir l'Allemagne en se donnant la mort.<br /><br />Il adhère au parti nazi et se voit confier la direction d'une ferme avec sa femme Elsie, où il vit des journées de dur labeur, mais paisibles. Puis, après la prise du pouvoir par Hitler, il entre dans les SS, n'ayant pourtant pas les critères requis pour y adhérer. Il accède à des fonctions de plus en plus importantes dans la hiérarchie SS, jusqu'à devenir commandant du camp d'Auschwitz. Ce camp, d'abord de concentration, puis d'extermination, devient le lieu de la lente et tâtonnante mise au point de l'Usine de Mort du village d'Auschwitz. Il y reçoit l'ordre du Reichsführer Himmler de supprimer 500 000 unités par an au lieu des ridicules 80 000 unités de Treblinka. Lang va s'attacher à accomplir la mission qui lui a été assignée : tuer le plus grand nombre de Juifs et éliminer le plus efficacement possible les cadavres. Après la guerre et la chute d'Hitler, il est emprisonné, puis condamné à la pendaison après son procès où il affirmera avoir seulement suivi les ordres, indiquant d'un air naturel qu'il a supervisé et participé activement au meurtre de « seulement » 2,5 millions de personnes au lieu des 3,5 millions prévus3.<br /><br />Tout au long du livre, il se montre incapable de sentiments et même d'action personnelle, car sa conduite lui a toujours été dictée par un chef en qui il portait une confiance totale. À la fin, on le sent cependant en colère se disant trahi par Himmler, qui, tel un lâche, s'est suicidé, et n'a ainsi pas voulu assumer son rôle dans l'extermination des Juifs, laissant Rudolf seul responsable de ses actes. Jusqu'au bout, il assume cependant son idée du chef, en répétant froidement et méthodiquement qu'il est le seul responsable de ce qui s'est passé à Auschwitz, et en énonçant sans difficulté les atrocités commises. Son seul moment de doute survient lorsque sa femme apprend ses activités, mais, ayant été choisi pour ses rares qualités de conscience il n'accorde pas d'importance à la morale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13724798372434047096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer78805717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15935940786031621346">La Mort Est Mon Métier = Death Is My Trade, Robert Merle<br/><br/><b>Death Is My Trade</b> is a 1952 French fictionalized biographical novel by Robert Merle. The protagonist, Rudolf Lang, was closely based on the real Rudolf Höß, commandant of the concentration camp Auschwitz.<br/><br/>The story begins in 1913, when Lang is 13 years old. His parents give him a harsh catholic education, to which he reacts badly. His unstable father, with whom the young Lang has an awkward relationship, wants him to become a priest. <br/><br/>At the </span>
  <span id="freeText15935940786031621346" style="display:none">La Mort Est Mon Métier = Death Is My Trade, Robert Merle<br /><br /><b>Death Is My Trade</b> is a 1952 French fictionalized biographical novel by Robert Merle. The protagonist, Rudolf Lang, was closely based on the real Rudolf Höß, commandant of the concentration camp Auschwitz.<br /><br />The story begins in 1913, when Lang is 13 years old. His parents give him a harsh catholic education, to which he reacts badly. His unstable father, with whom the young Lang has an awkward relationship, wants him to become a priest. <br /><br />At the age of fifteen, Lang starts a military career which leads in 1943 to the post of commandant of Auschwitz. At first a concentration camp, later an extermination camp, the camp, near town of Auschwitz, was the site of the <i>“slow and clumsy creation of a death factory”.</i> <br /><br />Lang works hard to achieve his mission: to kill as many Jews as possible, disposing of the bodies as efficiently as possible.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 1978 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: مرگ کسب‌ و کارِ من است؛ نویسنده: روبر مرل؛ مترجم احمد شاملو؛ تهران، کتاب زمان، چاپ دوم 1356؛ چاپ دیگر 1363؛ در شانزده و 368ص؛ چاپ چهارم در 460ص؛ انتشارات نگاه و زمانه، 1377؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، نگاه، 1388، در 415ص؛ شابک 9789646174313؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان فرانسوی - سده 20م<br /><br />مرگ کسب و کار من است، سرگذشت «رودلف هوس» است؛ او در این کتاب «رودلف لانگ» نام دارد؛ چرا که کتاب کل داستان زندگی این جلاد نیست، و تنها شامل بخش کاری وی، و در باره ی چند سال پایانی زندگی اوست؛ سال‌هایی که فرمانده، و مسئول اردوگاه آشویتس بود؛ و مسائل مربوط به زندگی شخصی او، به یاری خلاقیت نویسنده، و با نگاه بر زندگی نیروهای نازی است.لازم است یادآوری شود که در هنگام فرار، او با نام «فرانز لانگ»، زندگی می‌کرد<br /><br />آغاز داستان فضای کودکی «لانگ» است، که چگونه با پدری سخت‌گیر، بسیار فرمانبردار تربیت شد.پدری بسیار مذهبی، که او را نذر کلیسا کرده بود، اما رودلف، همیشه در قلب خود، عمویش را که یک افسر بود، می‌ستود.آرزوی او این بود، که همانند عموی خود، فردی نظامی شود، اما آن را غیرممکن می‌دید، تا زمانیکه رخدادی کوچک، مسیر زندگی او را تغییر داد.آن واقعه سبب اندوه ژرف او، و از دست دادن ایمانش شد؛ و خلأیی در دل او بوجود آورد.او در سن شانزده سالگی، با فرار از خانه، به ارتش پیوست، و با وجود سن کمش، به یاری اطاعت محض و انضباط، مدارج ترقی را طی کرد.به همین ترتیب او قسمت بیشتر زندگی خویش را، در جنگ جهانگیر نخست، صرف کرد، پس از اتمام جنگ، مدتی را به کارگری مشغول بود، تا زمانیکه به حزب نازی پیوست.او ماموریت‌های مختلفی را به عهده گرفت، و به دلیل قتل معلمی به دستور حزب، چند سال از عمر خویش را در زندان س‍‍‍‍‍‍پری کرد.پس از آزادی او همچنان به فعالیت‌های خود برای حزب ادامه داد.او را برای کار در مزرعه‌ ای گماردند.او توانست با آباد کردن مزرعه در زمان کوتاه، قدرت سازماندهی خود را نشان دهد.تا زمانی که او را به ریاست اردوگاه کار اجباری آشویتس منصوب کردند؛ و ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

  <u>Death Is My Trade</u>
</b><br><br><b>Rating : 4,5 Stars</b><br><br>A dark dark book.<br>Germany, first half of the 20th century. WW1 just finished, German are angry and ashamed to have lost this war, and the country is poorer than ever. The people ressent countries from the Alliance and most believe that soon they will get revenge by being obedient and faithful to their country. In this book we follow Rudolf Lang, from childhood until the end of his days. Raised in a very severe and strict way by his father who is former officer, he finally gets into the army at the age of 16. <br><blockquote>
  <i>"If a plea bites you, don't you kill them all?"</i>
</blockquote><br>He gets through horrible things for his age, and at the beginning of 1940's he is recruited to be with the S.S.<br>He becomes the leader of Auschwitz's extermination camp and he is the one who put the finishing touches to it, making it more efficient. <br>The worst part is that he is so obedient that not even once he thinks how immoral what he is doing is. He refuse to contest his leader, because it is not what germans do.<br><blockquote>
  <i>"At one point, the prosecutor shouted: "you killed 3,5 million people!" I asked to speak and said "I beg your pardon, I only killed 2,5 million." Whispers raised in the audience, and the prosecutor yelled that I should be ashamed of my cynicism. I have done nothing but to correct him on an erroneous data."</i>
</blockquote><br>The only part that bothered me was that some sentences were written in german, and I always had to move back and forth in my book to seek for the translation<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425814890i/13937190.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think that the hardest part was to hate Rudolf, at least like I should have.<br>I think that I'm not capable to make a relevant review of this book. <br>I think that you have to read it to fully understand how dark and twisted and obedient Rudolf was.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6746374992638318639">A rather chilling “autobiography” of the former Auschwitz commander. Demonstration of how the institutionalized evil can become an integral part of every human being. The book is often written in a strict diary style - where human beings are mere numbers and mass murder is described as solving mathematical exercise. Höss (under the pseudonym Lange) acts as a pedant, honest and hard worker; however he completely lacks emotional intelligence. He doesn’t enjoy killing, just wants to be effective an</span>
  <span id="freeText6746374992638318639" style="display:none">A rather chilling “autobiography” of the former Auschwitz commander. Demonstration of how the institutionalized evil can become an integral part of every human being. The book is often written in a strict diary style - where human beings are mere numbers and mass murder is described as solving mathematical exercise. Höss (under the pseudonym Lange) acts as a pedant, honest and hard worker; however he completely lacks emotional intelligence. He doesn’t enjoy killing, just wants to be effective and useful. At some point, the reader almost sympathize with him (unlike Himmler, Lange took full responsibility for everything that happened in Auschwitz). The author skilfully exploited his wide knowledge about the Holocaust and connected it with the knowledge of psychology. A powerful book, tough reading...</span>

  <span id="freeText2715303565461588006" style="display:none">Firstly, I should to say I've read "Man search for meaning" from Viktor Frankl who has been prisoner in the Auschwitz and this book which is called "Death is my trade" from Robert Merle about commander of the same prison. <br />The author of this book wrote it by reading about Nazi officers confessions and investigation about their life. This book has retrieved from Rudolf Höss life. <br />War in the word is that much dirty which I don't like to talk about it but I would like to talk about another side of this real tragedy that results in killed about 1.5 million(I'm not sure about the number) human during 5 years. <br />He always claimed that on his confession I just did my duty and I did the commands. <br />But really we as human what would be our duty in return to others? <br />I like this part of book which is communication between Rudolf and American Colonel in the prison. Honestly what is the difference between Rudolf Höss and that Bomber Pilot who attacked Hiroshima and Nagasaki? <br />The answer is, that side who is winner won't be blame and there are a lot of example like this in history! <br />Victorious and Defeated, both of them should be blame because of their results which have been killed many people around the world who killed because of ridiculous belief of idiots leaders. These days we are witnessed many inhumanity, especially in the Middle East and it's the dirty politics!<br />At the end I should add I don't have problem with any nationality, I respect to any flag but we should accept it our leader's hands are bloody. Before everything find your own ideology and instead take a gun, increase your knowledge by education. <br />Hope one day love replace the extremism. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132051680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4599105130904782923">This took me quite a while to finish. One reason was the style I never could really got into - which is a shame, since this is a really good book, good in the way the (true) horror grabs you and makes you wonder/shake your head at the "how" and "why". This is the (semi/somewhat) fictional biographical story about Rudolf Lang, who would be Rudolf Hoeß, the commander of Auschwitz concentration camp. The horror is real/has been real, and, needless to say, Lang/Hoeß is a messed up a character as it </span>
  <span id="freeText4599105130904782923" style="display:none">This took me quite a while to finish. One reason was the style I never could really got into - which is a shame, since this is a really good book, good in the way the (true) horror grabs you and makes you wonder/shake your head at the "how" and "why". This is the (semi/somewhat) fictional biographical story about Rudolf Lang, who would be Rudolf Hoeß, the commander of Auschwitz concentration camp. The horror is real/has been real, and, needless to say, Lang/Hoeß is a messed up a character as it gets. Gruesome, painful, very much so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4599105130904782923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1399338966" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399338966" />
    <a title="Ellstra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22481678-ellstra"><img alt="Ellstra" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

        <a title="Ellstra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellstra" href="/user/show/22481678-ellstra">Ellstra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399338966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3564210844901041192">Intriguing, breath-taking. This book shows horrors of World War II and people behind it into a completely different light. A book where the main character is the villain... or is he? Facts are interwoven with fiction so well you almost can't put it down. Fascinating and accurate depiction of mental illness. It shows how a parent can damage their child forever without ever beating it and that emotional abuse is just as real as the physical. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1692320267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692320267" />
    <a title="Ray" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51601315-ray"><img alt="Ray" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1692320267?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ray" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ray" href="/user/show/51601315-ray">Ray</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692320267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15794326266154575809">it was a slow book to read and I had to be patient as I was told that all the excitement came later, at the end. And it was true. It gave me goosebumps and creeped me out a bit because of all the horrible things he did. however, it was really different and refreshing to read a Nazi's perspective for I only read the other's side point of view. <br/>The writer's style is really easy to read and quite descriptive an precise.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2559133961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2559133961" />
    <a title="Benoît" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8593248-beno-t"><img alt="Benoît" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538568913p2/8593248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2559133961?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benoît" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benoît" href="/user/show/8593248-beno-t">Benoît</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2559133961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2339003656675461299">La Mort est mon Métier (Death is my Trade, 1952) is a fictionalized portrait of Rudolph Höss, who commanded the concentration camp of Auschwitz during its crucial years of extermination. It tells his life from what was known and from what he said of it in the memoirs he was instructed to write during his trial. As a commander, he personally designed the installations in Auschwitz, under direct order from Himmler (by far the most fascinatingly scary character in the book), and can be considered t</span>
  <span id="freeText2339003656675461299" style="display:none">La Mort est mon Métier (Death is my Trade, 1952) is a fictionalized portrait of Rudolph Höss, who commanded the concentration camp of Auschwitz during its crucial years of extermination. It tells his life from what was known and from what he said of it in the memoirs he was instructed to write during his trial. As a commander, he personally designed the installations in Auschwitz, under direct order from Himmler (by far the most fascinatingly scary character in the book), and can be considered to have assassinated 2.5 millions people, which is his estimate.<br /><br />The interest of the book of course lies between the psychological and moral question: what kind of conscience can you have when you organize mass killings, when you organize death ? I personally do not believe that following orders (the common defense) was all everyone thought there was to it. Still, you must probably come to believe it's a necessity over which you personally have no control and no responsibility, and you just focus on your own very modest life as soldier (in a bubble). Those questions are forever unresolved.<br /><br />The scenes in the camp are the most difficult but also the best, as frankly, I do not overly care about the character's background and relation to this unloving authoritative father. Merle is faithful at least, which is good, and he makes clear enough that Rudolph has no sensitivity for human life in the context of war (otherwise, he's just polite, reserved, weird in his matter-of-factedness). The scenes in Auschwitz are successful because Merle shows the terribleness and surreal absurdity of Rudolph Höss' zealous struggle to simply make his camp function and to bring Himmler's plans to reality. Which he does. And that is why he was chosen, as he said many times: he's good at organization. What is terrifying is that he apparently wasn't cynical, it's what he believed. For whatever it's worth, after showing absolute detachment during his trial, and while he could have no doubt over his eventual sentence, Höss apparently began to feel doubt about what he had done, about the rightfulness of the orders, and expressed a very late regret. Hard to believe, yes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2339003656675461299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2487014496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2487014496" />
    <a title="Dalma Vatai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82471557-dalma-vatai"><img alt="Dalma Vatai" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2487014496?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dalma Vatai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dalma Vatai" href="/user/show/82471557-dalma-vatai">Dalma Vatai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12210966-mesters-gem-a-hal-l">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2487014496&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2487014496" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4641578892006069700">Merle, in his fictional biography of Rudolf Hoess, the Commandant of Auschwitz, imagines Hoess as someone whose life was, from the very beginning, shaped by obedience. Obedience was the highest virtue in his world, and something without which he did not feel any sense of accomplishment or self-worth. Fictional Hoess (and very likely real-life Hoess as well) did not have his own thoughts, beliefs, feelings, emotions, etc., thus, his entire being was an embodiment of the commands he was given. Thi</span>
  <span id="freeText4641578892006069700" style="display:none">Merle, in his fictional biography of Rudolf Hoess, the Commandant of Auschwitz, imagines Hoess as someone whose life was, from the very beginning, shaped by obedience. Obedience was the highest virtue in his world, and something without which he did not feel any sense of accomplishment or self-worth. Fictional Hoess (and very likely real-life Hoess as well) did not have his own thoughts, beliefs, feelings, emotions, etc., thus, his entire being was an embodiment of the commands he was given. This conditioning comes from his father, who, I would argue, had the worst impact on Hoess of all people. His entire existence was determined by the kinds of commands he was given; this, coupled with the fervent nationalism and anti-Semitism of interwar Germany, proved lethal for millions of Jews and others. But nationalism and anti-Semitism in themselves would not have been enough to make Auschwitz the disaster that it was made to be; I believe the most crucial component was Hoess' pathological obsession with obeying commands and his being able to derive a sense of accomplishment from obeying commands only. I think it is also important to note that he never received love as a child: his parents did not provide him with love, care, or connection, so he was never able to build those things later in life. This helped him detach from the deaths of millions that happened before his very eyes; he was simply unable to connect to other people, and so unable to feel anything like love or sympathy towards them. <br />I believe this book is a crucial piece of the vast literature on the Holocaust, as it illuminates the psychological background of Hoess' seemingly incomprehensible inhumanity, and possibly that of many others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4641578892006069700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11483929732961848217" style="display:none">The book “Death Is My Trade” was an attempt to submerge into the mind of the man responsible for leading one of the death camps Auschwitz. His profile as a soldier just listening to the orders is I think quite accurate, but his lack of simple human emotions is really disturbing. The main character does not recognize humans sent to death as human beings, but as units he was assigned to take care of. His problem is not with the killing, but with getting rid of the bodies. He has no philosophical problems with the killing of more than a million people, his difficulties with this task are purely technical.<br />The main character is even with his lack of human trades quite believable. Author provides the story of his whole life, his problems with crazy father, his obsession with order and war, the presence and sympathy to NSDAP and also why he was chosen to lead the camp by Heinrich Himmler.<br />I can’t judge whether it’s an accurate mental description of the real Rudolf Höß, but it makes you think about this man a lot.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_8580616'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8580616-iskola-a-hat-ron"><img alt="Iskola a határon" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1279119047l/8580616._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KYGEDj8QocsonlG9z5PBfLvy0yoB7wa6Sv7CLxrbITilTUpe3hUxQi0t3ZR91DOY8IGLQ7xf6PKUQ+QVFqK4aw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

هرکدام نماینده‌ی طبقه‌ای از جامعه‌ی آن زمان ایران است. گیله مرد نماینده‌ی مردم ستم دیده‌ایست که راه مبارزه را در پیش گرفته اند. «محمد ولی وکیل باشی» مامور اول، نماد دولت است و مامور دوم، «مرد بلوچ» نماد گروهی از مردم ستم دیده است که راه حل عبور از این ظلم را در ظلم به دیگران می‌بیند.\n\nگیله مرد برشی کوتاه از داستان زندگی مردی روستایی است. دهقانی شورشی که علیه ظلم و ستم قیام کرده است. همسر گیله مرد را ماموران دولت کشته اند. داستان جایی میان جنگل‌های گیلان روایت می‌شود، جایی که دو مامور دولت گیله مرد را به پاسگاهی در فومن می‌برند.\n\nمامور اول، «محمدولی» مرد بدطینتی است و دائم گوشه و کنایه می‌زند و گیله مرد را آزار می‌دهد. اما مردم دوم در سکوت راه می‌‌رود. سکوتی که گیله مرد را کلافه کرده است.\n\nبخشی از داستان در ذهن گیله مرد می‌گذرد. او در فکر انتقام صغرا همسرش است و فکر بچه‌اش؛ بچه‌ی شش ماهه‌ای که داخل کومه جامانده و حالا گیله مرد نمی‌دانست چه بر سرش خواهد آمد. او تلاش می‌کند راهی برای فرار پیدا کند.\n\nبه موازات گیله مرد، مرد بلوچ ساکت هم در اندیشه زندگی خودش است. او را به زور به           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5590476120228174622">Born in Tebessa located in ,what was then, the French colony of Algeria. Robert Merle and his family moved to France in 1918. Merle wrote in many styles and won the Prix Goncourt for his novel Week-end à Zuydcoote. He has also written a 13 book series of historical novels, Fortune de France. Recreating 16th and 17th century France through the eyes of a fictitious Protestant doctor turned spy, he w</span>
  <span id="freeText5590476120228174622" style="display:none">Born in Tebessa located in ,what was then, the French colony of Algeria. Robert Merle and his family moved to France in 1918. Merle wrote in many styles and won the Prix Goncourt for his novel Week-end à Zuydcoote. He has also written a 13 book series of historical novels, Fortune de France. Recreating 16th and 17th century France through the eyes of a fictitious Protestant doctor turned spy, he went so far as to write it in the period's French making it virtually untranslatable.<br /><br />His novels Un animal doué de la raison (A Sentient Animal, 1967), a stark Cold War satire inspired by John Lilly's studies of dolphins and the Caribbean Crisis, and Malevil (1972), a post-apocalyptic story, were both translated into English and filmed, the former as Day of the Dolphin. The film The Day of the Dolphin bore very little resemblance to Merle's story.<br /><br />He died of a heart attack at his home La Malmaison in Grosrouvre near Paris.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5590476120228174622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
